Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the aromatic ring to stabilize the catalyst structure through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the carboxylic acid may enhance the reactivity of the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The presence of sulfur may contribute to the electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers containing a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may destabilize the catalyst or reduce its reactivity.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The formyl group may act as an electron-withdrawing group, reducing the effectiveness of the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2;$([OX2][c])]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']  # Rule 9: Simple aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[$([NX3H2][CX3](=O)[O-])][c]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[$([OX2H][CX4][OX2H])]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group
        ['[CX4]']  # Rule 9: Simple aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern `[$([OX2H][CX4][OX2H])]` should be refined to capture sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyl groups. Consider using a pattern that captures multiple hydroxyl groups in a cyclic structure, e.g., `[$([OX2H][CX4][OX2H])]` should be expanded to include cyclic structures with multiple hydroxyl groups.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 4, the SMARTS pattern `[SX2H]` is correct for a sulfanyl group. Ensure that it captures the presence of sulfur in the correct context.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS pattern `[CX4](F)(F)F` correctly captures a trifluoromethyl group. Ensure that it is applied correctly to identify low yield predictions.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern `[c][OX2][c]` should be refined to ensure it captures methoxy groups adjacent to aromatic rings. Consider using a more specific pattern, e.g., `[c]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1[OX2][c]`.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern `[CX3H]=[OX1]` correctly captures a formyl group. Ensure that it is applied correctly to identify low yield predictions.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern `[CX4]` is too broad and may capture any aliphatic carbon. Refine it to capture simple aliphatic chains without additional functional groups, e.g., `[CX4][CX4][CX4]`.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Review the SMILES strings and ensure that the SMARTS patterns are applied correctly to each SMILES. If a rule is not matching as expected, verify the SMARTS pattern and the SMILES structure for compatibility.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[$([NX3H2][CX3](=O)[O-])][c]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring
        ['[c]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1[CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[$([OX2H][CX4][OX2H])]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[SX2H]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 6: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[c]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1[OX2][c]'],  # Rule 7: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]']  # Rule 9: Simple aliphatic chain
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 7]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current validation accuracy of 0.514 is significantly lower than the previous reference accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. This suggests that the current rules are not effective enough in predicting the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The drop in validation accuracy indicates potential underfitting. The model may not be capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively, possibly due to overly simplistic or incorrect rules.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, Rule 6 and Rule 8 consistently have high positive SHAP values. This suggests that these rules might be overestimating the loading.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, Rule 6 and Rule 8 also show high negative SHAP values, indicating they might be underestimating the loading.

4. **Accuracy Improvements Interpretation:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is a significant opportunity for improvement. The rules need refinement to better capture the relationship between molecular features and catalyst loading.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - The SHAP analysis indicates that Rule 6 and Rule 8 are consistently contributing to incorrect predictions. This suggests that these rules may need to be revised or replaced to improve model performance.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Rules with High Positive SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 6**: Consider revising the impact of the trifluoromethyl group. It may not always lead to low yield, and its effect might be context-dependent. Investigate if there are specific conditions or additional features that modify its impact.
   - **Rule 8**: Re-evaluate the influence of the formyl group. It might not universally lead to low yield, and its interaction with other functional groups should be considered.

2. **Adjust Rules with High Negative SHAP Values:**
   - **Rule 6 and Rule 8**: These rules should be adjusted to account for cases where they underestimate the loading. Consider incorporating additional features or interactions that could influence the outcome.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Introduce more nuanced rules that consider the context and interactions between different functional groups. This could help in addressing the underfitting issue and improve the model's ability to generalize across different molecules.

4. **Iterative Refinement Using SHAP Insights:**
   - Use the SHAP analysis to identify patterns in the data that are not currently captured by the rules. This could involve exploring new features or modifying existing ones to better align with the experimental outcomes.

5. **Additional Considerations:**
   - Consider incorporating machine learning techniques to automatically identify and validate new rules or features that could improve the model's performance.
   - Regularly evaluate the model's performance on a separate test set to ensure that improvements in validation accuracy translate to better generalization.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the aromatic ring to stabilize the catalyst structure through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the carboxylic acid may enhance the reactivity of the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The presence of sulfur may contribute to the electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers containing a trifluoromethyl group (e.g., 4-[(2,2,2-trifluoroacetyl)amino]butanoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing nature of the trifluoromethyl group may destabilize the catalyst or reduce its reactivity.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid, 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The formyl group may act as an electron-withdrawing group, reducing the effectiveness of the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The presence of sulfur may contribute to the electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group combined with an electron-donating group (e.g., methoxy) on an aromatic ring may result in a balanced yield. The electron-donating group can mitigate the electron-withdrawing effect of the trifluoromethyl group.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group combined with an electron-donating group (e.g., amino) on an aromatic ring may result in a balanced yield. The electron-donating group can mitigate the electron-withdrawing effect of the formyl group.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with both electron-donating and electron-withdrawing groups on the same aromatic ring (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid with an additional methoxy group) can lead to high yield due to the stabilization of the catalyst through balanced electronic effects.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[c][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c][CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 7: Trifluoromethyl group with electron-donating group
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 8: Formyl group with electron-donating group
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 9: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][NX3+](=O)[OX1-]'],  # Rule 10: Electron-donating and withdrawing groups on aromatic ring
        ['[o]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 11: Benzofuran structure
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    elif i in [6, 7]:  # Rules predicting balanced yield
                        row.append(0)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])]` is intended to match amino acid structures with an aromatic ring. Consider using a more comprehensive pattern that captures the entire amino acid structure with an aromatic ring, such as `[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]`.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern `[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]` is meant to identify multiple hydroxyl groups in a sugar-like structure. This pattern may not be specific enough to capture the sugar-like structure. Consider using a pattern that captures the cyclic nature and multiple hydroxyl groups, such as `[C@H]1([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]1[O]`.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 5, the SMARTS pattern `[n]1ccccc1` is used to identify pyridine rings. This pattern is correct, but ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly parsed to identify pyridine structures.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS pattern `[c][OX2H1]` is intended to match methoxy groups adjacent to an aromatic ring. This pattern may not be specific enough. Consider using `[c][O][CH3]` to specifically match methoxy groups.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern `[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]` is intended to match simple aliphatic chains. This pattern may not be specific enough to exclude other functional groups. Consider using a pattern that explicitly excludes functional groups, such as `[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4;!$(C[!#6])]`.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern `[c][NX3+](=O)[OX1-]` is intended to match electron-donating and withdrawing groups on the same aromatic ring. This pattern may not capture all possible combinations. Consider using a more flexible pattern that allows for various electron-donating and withdrawing groups, such as `[c][NX3+](=O)[OX1-]` with additional substructure checks for electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Ensure that the SMARTS patterns are tested against a diverse set of SMILES strings to verify their accuracy and coverage. This can help identify any mismatches or missing matches in the feature matrix.

    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10]:  # Rules predicting high yield
                        row.append(1)
                    elif i in [6, 7]:  # Rules predicting balanced yield
                        row.append(0)
                    else:  # Rules predicting low yield
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the aromatic ring to stabilize the catalyst structure through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the carboxylic acid may enhance the reactivity of the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The presence of sulfur may contribute to the electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group combined with an electron-donating group (e.g., methoxy) on an aromatic ring may result in a balanced yield. The electron-donating group can mitigate the electron-withdrawing effect of the trifluoromethyl group.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a formyl group combined with an electron-donating group (e.g., amino) on an aromatic ring may result in a balanced yield. The electron-donating group can mitigate the electron-withdrawing effect of the formyl group.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with both electron-donating and electron-withdrawing groups on the same aromatic ring (e.g., 4-nitrobenzoic acid with an additional methoxy group) can lead to high yield due to the stabilization of the catalyst through balanced electronic effects.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]']` may not fully capture the presence of an aromatic ring in amino acid structures. Consider using a more specific pattern that includes aromatic rings, such as `['[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1']` to ensure the aromatic ring is detected.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS pattern `['[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])']` is too specific and may not match all sugar-like structures. Consider using a more general pattern for multiple hydroxyl groups, such as `['[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])']` to capture a broader range of sugar-like structures.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX4](F)(F)F']` does not account for the presence of an electron-donating group. Modify the pattern to include an electron-donating group, such as `['[c][CX4](F)(F)F', '[c][O][CH3]']`.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 8, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][CX3H]=O']` should be modified to include the presence of an electron-donating group. Consider using a pattern like `['[c][CX3H]=O', '[c][NX3]']` to ensure the electron-donating group is detected.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS pattern `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` may not accurately capture simple aliphatic chains. Consider using a more general pattern like `['[CX4][CX4][CX4]']` to match a wider range of aliphatic chains.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 10, the SMARTS pattern `['[c][NX3+](=O)[OX1-]']` should be modified to ensure it captures both electron-donating and electron-withdrawing groups on the same aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern like `['[c][NX3+](=O)[OX1-]', '[c][O][CH3]']`.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Ensure that the SMARTS patterns are tested against a diverse set of SMILES to verify their accuracy in capturing the intended chemical structures. This can help identify any mismatches or false negatives in the feature matrix.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the aromatic ring to stabilize the catalyst structure through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the carboxylic acid may enhance the reactivity of the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The presence of sulfur may contribute to the electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

**End of Rules**

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        '[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])]',  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring
        '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]',  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid group adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[OX2;$([r5]1@C(!@[OX2,NX3,SX2,FX1,ClX1,BrX1,IX1])@C@C(O)@C1),$([r6]1@C(!@[OX2,NX3,SX2,FX1,ClX1,BrX1,IX1])@C@C(O)@C(O)@C1)]',  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        '[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]',  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        '[n]1ccccc1',  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        '[c][OX2][C]',  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[c]1oc2ccccc2c1',  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        '[CX4][CX4][CX4]',  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        '[c][CX3H]=O',  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        '[C][OX2][C][C](=[O])[C]',  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        '[CX4](F)(F)F'  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule)):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        '[NX3H2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]',  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring
        '[c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]',  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid group adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)',  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        '[SX2H]',  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        '[n]1ccncc1',  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        '[c][c][OX2][C]',  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[c]1oc2ccccc2c1',  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        '[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]',  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        '[c][c][CX3H]=O',  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        '[C][OX2][C](=[O])[C]',  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        '[CX4](F)(F)F'  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule)):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS pattern '[c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' should be refined to ensure it captures carboxylic acid groups adjacent to aromatic rings. Consider using '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' to ensure the carboxylic acid is directly adjacent to the aromatic ring.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS '[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)' may not capture all sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyl groups. Consider using a more flexible pattern like '[C](O)[C](O)[C](O)' to account for different stereochemistry.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 5's SMARTS '[n]1ccncc1' is specific to pyridine but may miss other pyridine derivatives. Consider using a more general pattern like '[n]1ccccc1' to capture a broader range of pyridine structures.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS '[c][c][OX2][C]' may not accurately capture methoxy groups adjacent to aromatic rings. Consider using '[c][OX2][C]' to ensure the methoxy group is directly adjacent to the aromatic ring.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 8's SMARTS '[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]' may not accurately capture simple aliphatic chains. Consider using a more general pattern like '[CX4][CX4][CX4]' to capture varying chain lengths.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS '[c][c][CX3H]=O' may not fully capture formyl groups on aromatic rings. Consider using '[c][CX3H]=O' to ensure the formyl group is directly on the aromatic ring.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 10's SMARTS '[C][OX2][C](=[O])[C]' may not accurately capture ether linkages with electron-withdrawing groups. Consider using '[C][OX2][C](=[O])[C;!$([C][OX2])]' to ensure the presence of an electron-withdrawing group.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: Ensure that the SMARTS patterns are tested against a diverse set of SMILES to verify their accuracy in capturing the intended structures.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]',  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring
        '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]',  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid group adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[C](O)[C](O)[C](O)',  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structure
        '[SX2H]',  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        '[n]1ccccc1',  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        '[c][OX2][C]',  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[c]1oc2ccccc2c1',  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        '[CX4][CX4][CX4]',  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        '[c][CX3H]=O',  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        '[C][OX2][C](=[O])[C;!$([C][OX2])]',  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        '[CX4](F)(F)F'  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule)):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the aromatic ring to stabilize the catalyst structure through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the carboxylic acid may enhance the reactivity of the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The presence of sulfur may contribute to the electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]' does not accurately capture the presence of an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring. The pattern should be modified to include the aromatic ring explicitly, such as '[NX3][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][c]'.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' may not fully capture the carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring. Consider using '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' with additional constraints to ensure adjacency, such as '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]'.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: For Rule 3, the SMARTS '[C](O)[C](O)[C](O)' might not be specific enough for sugar-like structures. Consider using a more specific pattern that captures the cyclic nature of sugars, such as '[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)'.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4's SMARTS '[SX2H]' is correct for identifying sulfanyl groups, but ensure that the SMILES strings in the dataset are correctly interpreted to match this pattern.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5's SMARTS '[n]1ccccc1' correctly identifies pyridine rings. However, ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly interpreted to match this pattern.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: For Rule 6, the SMARTS '[c][OX2][C]' may not fully capture methoxy groups adjacent to aromatic rings. Consider using '[c][OX2][C;R]' to ensure the methoxy group is part of an aromatic system.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7's SMARTS '[c]1oc2ccccc2c1' is specific to benzofuran structures. Ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly interpreted to match this pattern.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS '[CX4][CX4][CX4]' may not be specific enough for simple aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern that specifies the absence of functional groups, such as '[CX4][CX4][CX4;!$([CX4][!#6])]'.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: For Rule 9, the SMARTS '[c][CX3H]=O' should be checked to ensure it captures formyl groups on aromatic rings accurately. Consider using '[c][CX3H]=O' with additional constraints to ensure the formyl group is directly attached to the aromatic ring.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS '[C][OX2][C](=[O])[C;!$([C][OX2])]' may not fully capture ether linkages with electron-withdrawing groups. Consider using a more specific pattern that captures the ether linkage and the electron-withdrawing group, such as '[C][OX2][C](=[O])[C;!$([C][OX2])][C;!$([C][OX2])]'.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11's SMARTS '[CX4](F)(F)F' correctly identifies trifluoromethyl groups. Ensure that the SMILES strings are correctly interpreted to match this pattern.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-aminobenzoic acid, (2S)-2-amino-3-phenylpropanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. This is likely due to the ability of the aromatic ring to stabilize the catalyst structure through π-π interactions.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the carboxylic acid may enhance the reactivity of the catalyst.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups, especially in a sugar-like structure (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups can facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The presence of sulfur may contribute to the electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

Rule Generator Message:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        '[NX3;$([N][c])]',  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine
        '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]',  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]',  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        '[SX2H]',  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        '[n]',  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        '[c][OX2][C]',  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        '[o1c2ccccc2]',  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        '[C][C]',  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        '[c][CX3H]=O',  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        '[C][OX2][C]',  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        '[CX4](F)(F)F',  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        '[C][OX2H]',  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        '[c][CH3]',  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        '[c][n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]',  # Rule 14: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
        '[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'  # Rule 15: Hydroxy group and formyl group on aromatic ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(rule)):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # High yield rules
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Low yield rules
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

** Start of Suggestions **
- ** Suggestion 1 **: Rule 1 in the code uses the SMARTS pattern '[NX3;$([N][c])]', which matches aromatic amines. However, the natural language rule specifies amino acids with specific stereochemistry and aromatic rings. The SMARTS should be updated to reflect the presence of an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry, such as '[C@@H](N)[C](=O)O' for amino acids.
- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2 in the code uses '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', which matches carboxylic acids but does not ensure adjacency to an aromatic ring or the presence of electron-withdrawing substituents. The SMARTS should be updated to include an aromatic ring and electron-withdrawing groups, such as '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'.
- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 3 uses '[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]', which matches multiple hydroxyl groups but does not ensure a sugar-like structure. The SMARTS should be updated to reflect sugar-like structures, such as '[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])'.
- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4 uses '[SX2H]', which matches sulfanyl groups but does not account for thioethers. The SMARTS should be updated to include thioethers, such as '[SX2]([C])[C]'.
- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5 uses '[n]', which matches pyridine rings correctly. However, ensure that the SMARTS pattern is specific enough to avoid false positives.
- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6 uses '[c][OX2][C]', which matches methoxy groups adjacent to aromatic rings. This is correct, but ensure the pattern is specific to the context described in the rule.
- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7 uses '[o1c2ccccc2]', which matches benzofuran structures. This is correct, but ensure the pattern is specific to the context described in the rule.
- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8 uses '[C][C]', which is too broad and matches any aliphatic chain. The SMARTS should be updated to reflect simple aliphatic chains without functional groups, such as '[C][C][C][C]'.
- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9 uses '[c][CX3H]=O', which matches formyl groups on aromatic rings. This is correct, but ensure the pattern is specific to the context described in the rule.
- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10 uses '[C][OX2][C]', which is too broad and does not ensure the presence of an electron-withdrawing group. The SMARTS should be updated to include electron-withdrawing groups, such as '[C][OX2][C](=O)[C]'.
- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11 uses '[CX4](F)(F)F', which matches trifluoromethyl groups correctly. This is correct, but ensure the pattern is specific to the context described in the rule.
- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12 uses '[C][OX2H]', which is too broad and does not ensure a long aliphatic chain. The SMARTS should be updated to reflect a long aliphatic chain with a hydroxy group, such as '[C][C][C][C][C][C][C][OX2H]'.
- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13 uses '[c][CH3]', which matches methyl groups on aromatic rings. This is correct, but ensure the pattern is specific to the context described in the rule.
- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14 uses '[c][n][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', which matches carboxylic acids and pyridine rings. This is correct, but ensure the pattern is specific to the context described in the rule.
- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15 uses '[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O', which matches hydroxy and formyl groups on aromatic rings. This is correct, but ensure the pattern is specific to the context described in the rule.
** End of Suggestions **

These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[c]', '[#6][NX3;$([H1]),$([H0][#6])]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[c][OX2;$([OX2][#6])]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[c]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n]1ccccc1[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])'],  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS pattern `['[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[c]', '[#6][NX3;$([H1]),$([H0][#6])]']` is intended to capture carboxylic acids adjacent to aromatic rings with electron-withdrawing groups. The current pattern may not fully capture the electron-withdrawing substituents. Consider adding specific patterns for common electron-withdrawing groups like nitro or bromo, such as `[$([c][C](=O)O)[$([c][Br]),$([c][N+](=O)[O-])]]`.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 3's SMARTS pattern `[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2]` is meant to identify multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures. This pattern may not fully capture the stereochemistry or the sugar-like structure. Consider using a more specific pattern that captures the cyclic nature and stereochemistry of sugars, such as `[$([C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)C(=O)O)]`.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4's SMARTS pattern `[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]` is intended to capture sulfanyl groups or thioethers. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures both sulfanyl and thioether groups, possibly by including patterns for both `[$([S][C])]` and `[$([C][S][C])]`.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5's SMARTS pattern `[n]1ccccc1` is correct for identifying pyridine rings. However, ensure that the rule logic correctly assigns a high yield prediction when this pattern is matched.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6's SMARTS pattern `[c][OX2;$([OX2][#6])]` is intended to capture methoxy groups adjacent to aromatic rings. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures the methoxy group and its position relative to the aromatic ring, such as `[$([c][O][C])]`.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7's SMARTS pattern `[c]1oc2ccccc2c1` is correct for identifying benzofuran structures. Ensure that the rule logic correctly assigns a high yield prediction when this pattern is matched.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS pattern `[CX4][CX4][CX4]` is intended to capture simple aliphatic chains. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures the lack of functional groups, possibly by using a more general pattern like `[$([C][C][C])]`.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9's SMARTS pattern `[c][CX3H]=[OX1]` is intended to capture formyl groups on aromatic rings. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures the formyl group and its position relative to the aromatic ring, such as `[$([c][C](=O)H)]`.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS pattern `[OX2][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[c]` is intended to capture ether linkages with electron-withdrawing groups. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures both the ether linkage and the electron-withdrawing group, possibly by using a more specific pattern like `[$([O][C](=O)[c])]`.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11's SMARTS pattern `[CX4](F)(F)F` is correct for identifying trifluoromethyl groups. Ensure that the rule logic correctly assigns a low yield prediction when this pattern is matched.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern `[CX4][OX2H]` is intended to capture hydroxy groups on long aliphatic chains. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures the hydroxy group and its position on the chain, possibly by using a more specific pattern like `[$([C][C][O]H)]`.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern `[c][CH3]` is intended to capture methyl groups on aromatic rings. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures the methyl group and its position relative to the aromatic ring, such as `[$([c][C]([H])([H])[H])]`.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern `[c][OX2H][CX3H]=[OX1]` is intended to capture hydroxy and formyl groups on aromatic rings. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures both groups and their positions relative to the aromatic ring, possibly by using a more specific pattern like `[$([c][O]H[C](=O)H)]`.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15's SMARTS pattern `[n]1ccccc1[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])` is intended to capture carboxylic acid and pyridine rings in the same molecule. Ensure that the pattern accurately captures both groups and their positions relative to each other, possibly by using a more specific pattern like `[$([n]1ccccc1[C](=O)O)]`.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[$([C@H](N)c1ccccc1)]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[$([c][C](=O)O)[$([c][Br]),$([c][N+](=O)[O-])]]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[$([C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)C(=O)O)]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        ['[$([S][C])]', '[$([C][S][C])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n]1ccccc1'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring
        ['[$([c][O][C])]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[$([C][C][C])]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[$([c][C](=O)H)]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[$([O][C](=O)[c])]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[$([C][C][O]H)]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[$([c][C]([H])([H])[H])]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[$([c][O]H[C](=O)H)]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[$([n]1ccccc1[C](=O)O)]'],  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to be struggling with effectiveness, as indicated by the low validation accuracy of 0.4286. This is a significant drop from previous accuracies, which were consistently around 0.76. The rules may not be capturing the necessary features to accurately predict the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting:**
   - The significant drop in validation accuracy suggests potential underfitting. The model may not be complex enough or the rules may not be capturing the necessary interactions and features to generalize well to the validation set.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 8 and Rule 10) are likely problematic. These rules may be overestimating the impact of certain features.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 5 and Rule 6) may be underestimating the impact of certain features.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest that there is room for improvement. The model's performance has decreased, indicating that the current rules may not be capturing the necessary complexity or interactions within the data.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules are consistently contributing to incorrect predictions. For example, Rule 8 and Rule 10 often have high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, suggesting these rules may need refinement.
   - Rules with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 5 and Rule 6, may need adjustment to better capture the features that lead to high experimental loadings.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Rules:**
   - Re-evaluate and refine Rule 8 and Rule 10, which are associated with high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings. Consider whether these rules are too broad or if they are capturing irrelevant features that lead to overestimation.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Rules:**
   - Adjust Rule 5 and Rule 6, which have high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings. These rules may need to be expanded or modified to better capture the features that lead to high experimental loadings.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - Consider introducing additional rules or modifying existing ones to capture more complex interactions. This could help address the underfitting issue and improve the model's ability to generalize to unseen data.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently contribute to incorrect predictions and adjust them based on the patterns observed in the SHAP values.

5. **Incorporate Additional Features:**
   - Explore incorporating additional features or interactions that may not be currently captured by the existing rules. This could involve considering new chemical properties or interactions that are relevant to the loading of modifiers on catalysts.

By addressing these areas, the rules can be refined to improve the model's accuracy and generalization, ultimately leading to better predictions of modifier loading on catalysts.

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid) tend to result in high yield. The methoxy group can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid) tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid) tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.
