Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;$([N][c])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]', '[#7,#8,#16,#17]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]', '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        ['[SX2H]', '[SX2]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS pattern '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]', '[#7,#8,#16,#17]' is too broad. It should specifically target carboxylic acids adjacent to aromatic rings with electron-withdrawing substituents. Consider refining the SMARTS to include these specific substituents.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 3's SMARTS pattern '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]' is not specific enough for sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyl groups. Consider using a pattern that captures the cyclic nature and multiple hydroxyl groups of sugars.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4's SMARTS pattern '[SX2H]', '[SX2]' should be checked to ensure it captures both sulfanyl groups and thioethers accurately. Consider using separate SMARTS for each group if necessary.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5's SMARTS pattern '[n][c]', '[OX2H]' does not accurately capture pyridine rings with electron-donating groups. Consider refining the pattern to specifically target pyridine rings and common electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]' should be refined to specifically target methoxy groups adjacent to aromatic rings, possibly using a pattern like '[c][OCH3]'.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7's SMARTS pattern '[c]1oc2ccccc2c1' is specific to benzofuran but should be checked for accuracy in capturing the structure across different SMILES.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS pattern '[CX4][CX4][CX4]' is too broad for simple aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern that captures the lack of functional groups more effectively.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9's SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3H]=O' should be checked to ensure it captures formyl groups on aromatic rings without electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS pattern '[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4]' should be refined to capture ether linkages with electron-withdrawing groups more accurately.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11's SMARTS pattern '[CX4](F)(F)F' is correct for trifluoromethyl groups but should be checked for context within the molecule.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern '[OX2H][CX4][CX4]' should be refined to capture hydroxy groups on long aliphatic chains more accurately.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern '[c][CH3]' should be checked to ensure it captures methyl groups on aromatic rings without additional electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O' should be refined to capture hydroxy and formyl groups on aromatic rings more accurately.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15's SMARTS pattern '[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]' should be checked to ensure it captures carboxylic acid and pyridine rings in the same molecule accurately.

** End of Suggestions **
---------------------------------------------------------------
Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;$([N][c])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]', '[#7,#8,#16,#17]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]', '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        ['[SX2H]', '[SX2]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS pattern '[CX4][CX4][CX4]' is too broad and may not accurately capture simple aliphatic chains without additional functional groups. Refine the pattern to exclude functional groups.
- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9's SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3H]=O' should be checked to ensure it captures formyl groups on aromatic rings without electron-donating groups.
- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS pattern '[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4]' may not effectively capture extensive ether linkages with electron-withdrawing groups. Consider refining the pattern to include these features.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern '[c][CH3]' should be checked to ensure it captures methyl groups on aromatic rings without additional electron-donating groups.
- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O' should be checked to ensure it captures hydroxy and formyl groups on aromatic rings.
- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15's SMARTS pattern '[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]' should be checked to ensure it captures carboxylic acid and pyridine rings in the same molecule without additional stabilizing groups.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;!$([N][!C])][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid with aromatic ring
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]', '[#6][NX3](=O)[OX1-]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid with aromatic ring
        ['[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]', '[OX2H][CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['[n][c][OX2H1]', '[n][c][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2][c]', '[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1', '[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]', '[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O', '[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]', '[OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F', '[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4]', '[OX2H][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]', '[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O', '[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;!$([N][!C])][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid with aromatic ring
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][N+](=O)[O-]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][Br]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H](=O)O'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2][c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Extensive ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 11 **: For Rule 11, the SMARTS pattern '[CX4](F)(F)F' accurately captures the trifluoromethyl group, but ensure that it is used in the correct context where no compensating electron-donating groups are present.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern '[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4]' may not fully capture the presence of a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain. Consider using a more specific pattern that captures the essence of this structure.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: For Rule 13, the SMARTS pattern '[c][CH3]' may not fully capture the presence of a methyl group on an aromatic ring. Ensure that the pattern accounts for the specific positioning of the methyl group.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O' may not fully capture the presence of a hydroxy group and a formyl group on an aromatic ring. Consider refining the pattern to include these specific features.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: For Rule 15, the SMARTS pattern '[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]' may not fully capture the presence of a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule. Ensure that the pattern accounts for the specific positioning of these groups.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;!$([N][!C])][CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid with aromatic ring
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][N+](=O)[O-]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][Br]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H]([OH])[C@H](=O)O'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c][OX2H1]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2][c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Extensive ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3H2+0,NX4H3+;$([N][c])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[OX2H]', '[c]', '[#7,#8,#9,#17]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]', '[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[SX2;$([H0]([#6])[c]),$([H0]([!#6])[c])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX4H3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[OX2H]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[C@H](N)[c]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring and stereochemistry
        ['[c][CX3](=[OX1])[OX2H][#7,#8,#9,#17]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        ['[SX2H;$([SX2H][CX4;!$(C([SX2H])~[O,S,#7,#15])])]', '[SX2;$([H0]([#6])[c]),$([H0]([!#6])[c])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OCH3][c][OCH3]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2][#7,#8,#9,#17]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX4H3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[OX2H]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[C@H](N)[c;R]'],  # Rule 1: Amino acid structure with aromatic ring and stereochemistry
        ['[c][CX3](=[OX1])[OX2H]', '[c][CX3](=[OX1])[OX2H][N+](=O)[O-]', '[c][CX3](=[OX1])[OX2H][Br]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures
        ['[SX2H]', '[SX2][CX4]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c]', '[n][c][c][c][c][c][OH]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OCH3][c][OCH3]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX4H3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=[OX1]'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3;$([R0][#6]),$([H1R0])](=[OX1])[OX2H]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;$([N][c])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]', '[$([Br]),$([N+](=O)[O-])]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2H]', '[SX2]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n]1ccccc1', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy groups on aromatic ring
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]', '[$([F]),$([Cl]),$([Br]),$([I])]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n]1ccccc1', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

The current pattern may not fully capture the adjacency requirement.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: For Rule 4, the SMARTS pattern '[SX2H]', '[SX2]' may not fully capture the presence of a sulfanyl group or thioether. Ensure the pattern is specific enough to distinguish these groups from other sulfur-containing functionalities.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5's SMARTS pattern '[n]1ccccc1', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]' does not accurately reflect the requirement for a pyridine ring with electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions. Consider revising the pattern to include positional specificity for electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]' should be revised to accurately capture methoxy groups on an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: For Rule 7, the SMARTS pattern 'c1oc2ccccc2c1' should be checked to ensure it accurately captures the benzofuran structure. Verify that the pattern matches the intended structure without false positives.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS pattern '[CX4][CX4][CX4]' may not accurately capture simple aliphatic chains. Consider using a more general pattern that captures aliphatic chains without additional functional groups.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9's SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3H]=O' should be checked to ensure it captures formyl groups on aromatic rings without electron-donating groups. Verify the pattern's specificity.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS pattern '[OX2][CX4][OX2]', '[$([F]),$([Cl]),$([Br]),$([I])]' should be revised to accurately capture ether linkages with electron-withdrawing groups, especially when the ether linkage is extensive.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11's SMARTS pattern '[CX4](F)(F)F' should be checked to ensure it accurately captures trifluoromethyl groups without compensating electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern '[CX4][OX2H]' may not fully capture hydroxy groups on long aliphatic chains. Consider using a pattern that captures the chain length and isolated nature of the hydroxy group.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern '[c][CH3]' should be checked to ensure it captures methyl groups on aromatic rings without additional electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H]', '[c][CX3H]=O' should be revised to accurately capture hydroxy and formyl groups on aromatic rings, ensuring the pattern reflects the intended structure.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15's SMARTS pattern '[n]1ccccc1', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H]' should be checked to ensure it captures carboxylic acid groups and pyridine rings in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;$([N][c])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c]', '[$([Br]),$([N+](=O)[O-])]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 3: Multiple hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2H]', '[SX2]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n]1ccccc1', '[OX2H]', '[OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy groups on aromatic ring
        ['c1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2]', '[$([F]),$([Cl]),$([Br]),$([I])]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with electron-withdrawing group
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[CX4][OX2H]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n]1ccccc1', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

### Performance Evaluation of Current Rules

1. **Effectiveness of Current Rules:**
   - The current rules seem to be struggling with effectiveness, as indicated by the validation accuracy of 0.4571, which is significantly lower than the previous reference accuracies (0.76). This suggests that the rules may not be capturing the underlying patterns in the data effectively.

2. **Overfitting/Underfitting Assessment:**
   - The consistent low validation accuracy across iterations suggests potential underfitting. The model may not be complex enough or the rules may not be capturing the necessary features to differentiate between high and low loading effectively.

3. **Discrepancies Analysis:**
   - For molecules where the predicted loading is high but the experimental value is low, rules with high positive SHAP values (e.g., Rule 9 and Rule 11) are likely problematic. These rules may be overestimating the contribution of certain features.
   - Conversely, for molecules where the predicted loading is low but the experimental value is high, rules with high negative SHAP values (e.g., Rule 8 and Rule 6) may be underestimating the contribution of certain features.

4. **Accuracy Improvements:**
   - The current accuracy metrics suggest limited improvement potential with the existing rules. The model's performance has not shown significant improvement across iterations, indicating that the rules may need substantial refinement or re-evaluation.

5. **Insights from SHAP Analysis:**
   - SHAP analysis indicates that certain rules (e.g., Rule 9 and Rule 11) consistently contribute to overestimated loadings, while others (e.g., Rule 8 and Rule 6) contribute to underestimated loadings. This suggests a need to refine these rules to better capture the true impact of the features they represent.

### Recommendations for Improvement

1. **Refine Overestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Re-evaluate and refine rules with high positive SHAP values for overestimated loadings, such as Rule 9 and Rule 11. Consider incorporating additional features or modifying the conditions under which these rules apply to better align with experimental outcomes.

2. **Adjust Underestimated Loading Rules:**
   - Modify rules with high negative SHAP values for underestimated loadings, such as Rule 8 and Rule 6. Explore additional interactions or features that may enhance the predictive power of these rules.

3. **Improve Generalization:**
   - To address potential underfitting, consider increasing the complexity of the model or incorporating additional features that may capture more nuanced patterns in the data. This could involve exploring new chemical properties or interactions not currently covered by the rules.

4. **Iterative Refinement:**
   - Use insights from SHAP analysis to iteratively refine the rules. Focus on rules that consistently show high SHAP values (positive or negative) and explore ways to adjust them to better reflect the experimental data.

5. **Incorporate Domain Knowledge:**
   - Leverage domain expertise to identify potential new rules or modify existing ones. Consider chemical properties or interactions that may not be currently captured but could influence catalyst loading.

By implementing these recommendations, the rules can be refined to improve the model's accuracy and better align predictions with experimental outcomes.

    Target Name: yield
