    Current_Rules:
    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group adjacent to an aromatic ring, especially with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid), are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures, considering different stereoisomers (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid), tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group directly adjacent to an aromatic ring with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures with specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid) tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;$([N][c])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]', '[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyls
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX4;!$(C(S)~[O,S,#7,#15])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2][c]', '[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Extensive ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][n][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures with specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid) tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern `['[NX3;$([N][c])]', '[c]']` does not accurately capture the requirement for an aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry. The SMARTS should be refined to include stereochemistry and aromatic ring presence, such as `['[C@H](N)[c]']`.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS `['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]']` should be adjusted to focus on carboxylic acid groups adjacent to aromatic rings with electron-withdrawing groups. Consider using `['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]']` and ensure electron-withdrawing groups are specified.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 3's SMARTS `['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]', '[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])']` should be revised to better capture sugar-like structures with multiple hydroxyls and specific stereochemistry. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])']`.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4's SMARTS `['[SX2H]', '[CX4;!$(C(S)~[O,S,#7,#15])]']` should be checked to ensure it captures both sulfanyl groups and thioethers. Consider using `['[SX2]', '[CX4;!$(C(S)~[O,S,#7,#15])]']`.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5's SMARTS `['[n][c][c][c][c][c]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]']` should be refined to ensure it captures pyridine rings with electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions. Consider using `['[n][c][c][c][c][c]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]']` with specific positions for electron-donating groups.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6's SMARTS `['[c][OX2][c]', '[c][OX2][c]']` should be adjusted to ensure it captures methoxy groups adjacent to aromatic rings, especially when multiple methoxy groups are present. Consider using `['[c][OX2][c]', '[c][OX2][c]']` with specific positions for methoxy groups.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7's SMARTS `['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1']` should be checked to ensure it captures benzofuran structures accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1']`.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` should be revised to ensure it captures simple aliphatic chains accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']`.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9's SMARTS `['[c][CX3H]=O']` should be checked to ensure it captures formyl groups on aromatic rings accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[c][CX3H]=O']`.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS `['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]']` should be revised to ensure it captures extensive ether linkages with electron-withdrawing groups accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]']`.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11's SMARTS `['[CX4](F)(F)F']` should be checked to ensure it captures trifluoromethyl groups accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[CX4](F)(F)F']`.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS `['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` should be revised to ensure it captures hydroxy groups on long aliphatic chains accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']`.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS `['[c][CH3]']` should be checked to ensure it captures methyl groups on aromatic rings accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[c][CH3]']`.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS `['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O']` should be revised to ensure it captures hydroxy and formyl groups on aromatic rings accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O']`.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15's SMARTS `['[c][n][CX3](=O)[OX2H]']` should be checked to ensure it captures carboxylic acid and pyridine rings accurately. Consider using a more specific pattern like `['[c][n][CX3](=O)[OX2H]']`.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[C@H](N)[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyls
        ['[SX2]', '[CX4;!$(C(S)~[O,S,#7,#15])]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2][c]', '[c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Extensive ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][n][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group directly adjacent to an aromatic ring with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures with specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid) tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

Matrix Checker Message:
** Start of Suggestions **

- ** Suggestion 1 **: For Rule 1, the SMARTS pattern '[C@H](N)[c]' may not fully capture the requirement of an aromatic ring with specific stereochemistry. Consider using a more specific pattern that includes the aromatic ring and stereochemistry, such as '[C@H](N)[c]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1'.

- ** Suggestion 2 **: Rule 2's SMARTS patterns '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]' and '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]' do not fully capture the requirement of electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups. Consider adding patterns for these specific substituents, such as '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H][c][N+](=O)[O-]' or '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H][c]Br'.

- ** Suggestion 3 **: Rule 3's SMARTS pattern '[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])' may not fully capture the sugar-like structure. Consider using a pattern that includes the cyclic nature of sugars, such as '[C@H]1([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]1([O])'.

- ** Suggestion 4 **: Rule 4's SMARTS patterns '[SX2]' and '[CX4;!$(C(S)~[O,S,#7,#15])]' may not fully capture the presence of a sulfanyl group or thioether. Consider using a more specific pattern that includes the sulfur atom bonded to carbon, such as '[CX4][SX2][CX4]'.

- ** Suggestion 5 **: Rule 5's SMARTS patterns '[n][c][c][c][c][c]' and '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]' may not fully capture the requirement of a pyridine ring with electron-donating groups. Consider using a pattern that includes specific electron-donating groups, such as '[n][c][c][c][c][c][OX2H]' for a pyridine with a hydroxy group.

- ** Suggestion 6 **: Rule 6's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2][c]' is too generic and may not capture the requirement of methoxy groups adjacent to an aromatic ring. Consider using a more specific pattern, such as '[c][OX2][c][OX2][c]' for multiple methoxy groups.

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7's SMARTS pattern '[c]1oc2ccccc2c1' may not fully capture the benzofuran structure. Consider using a pattern that includes the oxygen atom in the furan ring, such as '[c]1oc2ccccc2o1'.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS pattern '[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]' may not fully capture the requirement of a simple aliphatic chain. Consider using a pattern that includes a longer chain, such as '[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'.

- ** Suggestion 9 **: Rule 9's SMARTS pattern '[c][CX3H]=O' may not fully capture the requirement of a formyl group on an aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern that includes the aromatic ring, such as '[c][CX3H]=O[c]'.

- ** Suggestion 10 **: Rule 10's SMARTS pattern '[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]' may not fully capture the requirement of an extensive ether linkage with an electron-withdrawing group. Consider using a pattern that includes specific electron-withdrawing groups, such as '[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'.

- ** Suggestion 11 **: Rule 11's SMARTS pattern '[CX4](F)(F)F' is correct for a trifluoromethyl group, but ensure that it is used in the context of the entire molecule to determine its effect on yield.

- ** Suggestion 12 **: Rule 12's SMARTS pattern '[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]' may not fully capture the requirement of a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain. Consider using a pattern that includes a longer chain, such as '[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'.

- ** Suggestion 13 **: Rule 13's SMARTS pattern '[c][CH3]' may not fully capture the requirement of a methyl group on an aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern that includes the aromatic ring, such as '[c][CH3][c]'.

- ** Suggestion 14 **: Rule 14's SMARTS pattern '[c][OX2H][CX3H]=O' may not fully capture the requirement of a hydroxy and formyl group on an aromatic ring. Consider using a pattern that includes the aromatic ring, such as '[c][OX2H][c][CX3H]=O'.

- ** Suggestion 15 **: Rule 15's SMARTS pattern '[c][n][CX3](=O)[OX2H]' may not fully capture the requirement of a carboxylic acid and pyridine ring. Consider using a pattern that includes the pyridine ring, such as '[c][n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'.

** End of Suggestions **

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[C@H](N)[c]1[cH][cH][cH][cH][cH]1'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H][c][N+](=O)[O-]', '[c][CX3](=O)[OX2H][c]Br'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[C@H]1([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]([O])[C@H]1([O])'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with multiple hydroxyls
        ['[CX4][SX2][CX4]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2][c][OX2][c]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2o1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O[c]'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 10: Extensive ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3][c]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H]'],  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group directly adjacent to an aromatic ring with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures with specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid) tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group directly adjacent to an aromatic ring with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures with specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid) tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[NX3;$([N][c])]', '[c]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]', '[c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[OX2H][CX4;!$(C(O)(O)[!#6])][OX2H]', '[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2H]', '[CX3](=O)[OX2H1]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H]', '[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df

- ** Suggestion 7 **: Rule 7's SMARTS `['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1']` is correct for benzofuran structures, but ensure it is applied correctly in the code logic.

- ** Suggestion 8 **: Rule 8's SMARTS `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` should be adjusted to better capture simple aliphatic chains, possibly using `['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]']` to ensure longer chains are detected.

Code for rules:
def rule2matrix(smiles_list):
    rules = [
        ['[$([NX3;$([N]([c])[c])][C@H])]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry
        ['[$([CX3](=O)[OX2H1][c][c][c][c][c][c][NX3;$([N]([c])[c])])]'],  # Rule 2: Carboxylic acid adjacent to aromatic ring with EWG
        ['[$([C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O)[C@H](O))]'],  # Rule 3: Sugar-like structure with hydroxyl groups
        ['[SX2H]', '[SX2]'],  # Rule 4: Sulfanyl group or thioether
        ['[n][c][c][c][c][c][c][OX2H]'],  # Rule 5: Pyridine ring with electron-donating groups
        ['[c][OCH3]'],  # Rule 6: Methoxy group adjacent to aromatic ring
        ['[c]1oc2ccccc2c1'],  # Rule 7: Benzofuran structure
        ['[CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 8: Simple aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 9: Formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4][OX2][CX4]'],  # Rule 10: Ether linkage with EWG
        ['[CX4](F)(F)F'],  # Rule 11: Trifluoromethyl group
        ['[OX2H][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4][CX4]'],  # Rule 12: Hydroxy group on long aliphatic chain
        ['[c][CH3]'],  # Rule 13: Methyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[c][OX2H][c][CX3H]=O'],  # Rule 14: Hydroxy and formyl group on aromatic ring
        ['[n][c][c][CX3](=O)[OX2H1]']  # Rule 15: Carboxylic acid and pyridine ring
    ]
    results = []
    for smi in smiles_list:
        mol = Chem.MolFromSmiles(smi)
        if mol is None:
            results.append([0] * len(rules))
            continue
        row = []
        for i, rule in enumerate(rules):
            try:
                if all(mol.HasSubstructMatch(Chem.MolFromSmarts(r)) for r in rule):
                    if i in [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6]:  # Rules with high prediction
                        row.append(1)
                    else:  # Rules with low prediction
                        row.append(-1)
                else:
                    row.append(0)
            except:
                row.append(0)
        results.append(row)
    df = pd.DataFrame(results, columns=[f'Rule {i+1}' for i in range(len(rules))])
    return df
---------------------------------------------------------------
Current rules:
**Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group directly adjacent to an aromatic ring with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures with specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid) tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

**End of Rules**---------------------------------------------------------------

    rules = [
        ['[$([NX3;$([N]([c])[c])][C@H])]'],  # Rule 1: Aromatic amine with specific stereochemistry

The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.

    **Start of Rules**

- **Rule 1**: Modifiers containing an amino acid structure with an aromatic ring and specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2S)-2-aminopentanedioic acid, (2R)-2-amino-3-(1H-indol-3-yl)propanoic acid) tend to result in a high yield. The stereochemistry and aromatic ring can enhance π-π interactions and stabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 2**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group directly adjacent to an aromatic ring with electron-withdrawing substituents like nitro or bromo groups (e.g., 4-(bromomethyl)benzoic acid, 4-nitrobenzoic acid) are associated with high yield. These substituents can enhance the reactivity of the catalyst through electron-withdrawing effects.

- **Rule 3**: Modifiers containing multiple hydroxyl groups in sugar-like structures with specific stereochemistry (e.g., (2R,3S,4R,5R)-2,3,4,5,6-pentahydroxyhexanoic acid) tend to lead to high yield. The multiple hydroxyl groups facilitate hydrogen bonding, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 4**: Modifiers with a sulfanyl group or thioether (e.g., 3-sulfanylpropanoic acid) are associated with high yield. The sulfur-containing groups contribute to electron-donating ability, enhancing catalyst performance.

- **Rule 5**: Modifiers with a pyridine ring and additional electron-donating groups at ortho or para positions (e.g., pyridine-3-carboxylic acid, 4-pyridin-4-ylbutanoic acid) generally result in high yield. The nitrogen in the pyridine ring can coordinate with metal centers, potentially stabilizing the catalyst, especially when electron-donating groups are present.

- **Rule 6**: Modifiers with a methoxy group adjacent to an aromatic ring, particularly when multiple methoxy groups are present and positioned ortho or para to each other (e.g., 4-(3,4-dimethoxyphenyl)-4-oxobutanoic acid), tend to result in high yield. The methoxy groups can donate electrons through resonance, potentially enhancing catalyst stability.

- **Rule 7**: Modifiers with a benzofuran structure (e.g., 1,3-dioxo-2-benzofuran-5-carboxylic acid) tend to result in high yield. The benzofuran ring can provide additional π-π interactions and electron delocalization, stabilizing the catalyst.

- **Rule 8**: Modifiers with a simple aliphatic chain and no additional functional groups (e.g., 7-aminoheptanoic acid, 8-aminooctanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of functional groups may limit interactions with the catalyst.

- **Rule 9**: Modifiers with a formyl group on an aromatic ring without any electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-formylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing nature of the formyl group may destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 10**: Modifiers with an ether linkage combined with an electron-withdrawing group, especially when the ether linkage is extensive (e.g., 2-[2-(2-methoxyethoxy)ethoxy]acetic acid), tend to result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing effect may reduce the catalyst's reactivity.

- **Rule 11**: Modifiers with a trifluoromethyl group without compensating electron-donating groups (e.g., 2,2,3,3,4,4,5,5,5-nonafluoropentanoic acid) are associated with low yield. The strong electron-withdrawing effect can destabilize the catalyst.

- **Rule 12**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on a long aliphatic chain (e.g., 7-hydroxyheptanoic acid) generally result in low yield. The isolated hydroxy group may not sufficiently interact with the catalyst to enhance yield.

- **Rule 13**: Modifiers with a methyl group on an aromatic ring without additional electron-donating groups (e.g., 4-methylbenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The lack of significant electron-donating effects may limit catalyst stabilization.

- **Rule 14**: Modifiers with a hydroxy group on an aromatic ring and a formyl group (e.g., 5-formyl-2-hydroxybenzoic acid) generally result in low yield. The electron-withdrawing formyl group may counteract the potential stabilizing effect of the hydroxy group.

- **Rule 15**: Modifiers with a carboxylic acid group and a pyridine ring in the same molecule, especially when no additional stabilizing groups are present (e.g., 4-pyridin-4-ylbenzoic acid), tend to result in low yield. The combination of these groups may lead to competitive binding or destabilization of the catalyst.
